Krewe of Rex invitation, 1881.	Krewe of Rex (Organization)	1881	Krewe of Rex (Organization); Balls (Parties)--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.; New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.		The Rex Organization was founded in 1872 in an effort to entertain Russia's Grand Duke Romanoff during his visit to the city, to attract visitors to New Orleans, and to provide a daytime parade as an alternative to the rowdy processions that had come to characterize Mardi Gras celebrations.  The following year, it began the tradition of holding a ball and selecting a Queen of Carnival.   Rex continues its parade is held on the Mardi Gras day. Atlanteans invitation, 1913.	Atlanteans (Organization)	1913	Atlanteans (Organization); New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; Balls (Parties)--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	Invitation ; 11 x 19 cm.	The Atlanteans were a Carnival organization founded in 1891.  They held masked balls and presented costumed tableaux.  Thomas Sloo, from whose papers these costume designs are taken, was a member of the organization.  Sloo was a partner in the firms of Baker, Sloo and Company and Whitney and Sloo Company of New Orleans, Louisiana. These companies manufactured saddlery, harnesses, and collars. Rex medal, 1880.	Krewe of Rex (Organization)	1880	Krewe of Rex (Organization); New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	Medal ; 8 x 8 cm.	Medals such as these were worn by members of the Rex court.  This one is found among the papers of Captain Thomas P. Leathers, a New Orleans steamboat master and owner.  The Rex Organization was founded in 1872 in an effort to entertain Russia's Grand Duke Romanoff during his visit to the city, to attract visitors to New Orleans, and to provide a daytime parade as an alternative to the rowdy processions that had come to characterize Mardi Gras celebrations.  The following year, it began the tradition of holding a ball and selecting a Queen of Carnival.   Rex continues; its parade is held on  Mardi Gras day. Sidney Arbour, Jr. New Orleans Mardi Gras album pages, 1935.	Arbour, Sidney Vincent, 1914-2011.	1935	New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; New Orleans (La.)--Photographs.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	Photograph album : b&w ; 8.5 x 11 in.	Selected pages from a larger album kept by Sidney Arbour, Jr. depict New Orleans during Mardi Gras, specifically the Rex Parade, Canal Street, and crowds.  Many provide a birds eye view of the festivities. Sidney Vincent Arbour, Jr., a prominent resident of Baton Rouge, La., was born Jan. 7, 1914.  He attended Catholic High in Baton Rouge, St. Stanislaus in Bay St. Louis, and Louisiana State University.   A veteran of World War II, he worked at Standard Oil in Baton Rouge as a reseacher and also developed real estate.	Louisiana State University Libraries, Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	Finding aid: http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special/findaid/5075.pdf	X:31 box 7	Sidney V. Atlanteans Dance Card 1898	Atlanteans (Organization)	1898	Atlanteans (Organization); New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; Balls (Parties)--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	Dance card ; 13 cm.	The Atlanteans were a Carnival organization founded in 1891.  They held masked balls and presented costumed tableaux.  Thomas Sloo, from whose papers these costume designs are taken, was a member of the organization.  Sloo was a partner in the firms of Baker, Sloo and Company and Whitney and Sloo Company of New Orleans, Louisiana. These companies manufactured saddlery, harnesses, and collars. Spanish Town Mardi Gras photographs, circa 1970s.	Chandler, Thomas W.	1970?-1980?	Spanish Town (Baton Rouge, La.); Baton Rouge (La.)--Social life and customs.; Carnival--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.	Contact sheets ; 10 x 8 in.	The Spanish Town Mardi Gras Parade began in 1981 and traditionally features bawdy or politically-themed floats that reference current events.  These photographs were taken by Thomas W. Chandler for his 1985 LSU landscape architecture thesis, in which he surveyed and analyzed Spanish Town. Located between the State Capitol and Interstate 110 and bounded on the north and south by State Capitol Drive and Main St., respectively, Spanish Town is considered the oldest neighborhood in Baton Rouge. It was commissioned in 1805 as a settlement for Canary Islanders when Baton Rouge was still held by the Spanish .  In the 20th and 21st-centuries, it has been known for its socio-economic diversity and sense of community. Costume sketches, circa 1900.		1900?	Atlanteans (Organization); Carnival costume--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	4 costume sketches ; 26 x 18 cm.	The Atlanteans were a Carnival organization founded in 1891.  They held masked balls and presented costumed tableaux.  Thomas Sloo, from whose papers these costume designs are taken, was a member of the organization.  Sloo was a partner in the firms of Baker, Sloo and Company and Whitney and Sloo Company of New Orleans, Louisiana. These companies manufactured saddlery, harnesses, and collars. J. Bennett Johnston papers Mardi Gras items, 1974, 1983.		1974; 1983	Carnival--Washington (D.C.); Balls (Parties)--Washington (D.C.); Johnston, J. Bennett (John Bennett), 1932-; Edwards, Edwin W.	Photographs ; 28 X 33 cm or smaller.	The Washington Mardi Gras Ball began as a way for Louisianans living in Washington to enjoy the traditional Mardi Gras festivities away from home.  After sporadic celebrations in the 1930s and 1940s organized by the Louisiana State Society, a D.C. social organization of native and adopted Louisianans, the ball has been held annually since 1953.  The chair of the event is chosen from the state’s congressional delegation.  In 1957, Senator Russell Long was chair, and in an effort to enliven the party, he created the Mystick Krewe of Louisianians.  Twenty years later the Krewe was incorporated as a non-profit organization and continues as the official sponsor.  The Washington Mardi Gras has grown to a three-day series of events that highlight the state’s food and culture, hosted by Louisiana’s members of Congress.  It features multiple parties, attendance of queens of Louisiana’s festivals, and the presentation of the king and queen and Mardi Gras princesses, most of whom are drawn from Louisiana families.  The ball is completely self-sustaining with costs covered by the sale of tickets, corporate donations and krewe memberships. The Washington Mardi Gras Ball began as a way for Louisianans living in Washington to enjoy the traditional Mardi Gras festivities away from home.  After sporadic celebrations in the 1930s and 1940s organized by the Louisiana State Society, a D.C. social organization of native and adopted Louisianans, the ball has been held annually since 1953.  The chair of the event is chosen from the state’s congressional delegation.  In 1957, Senator Russell Long was chair, and in an effort to enliven the party, he created the Mystick Krewe of Louisianians.  Twenty years later the Krewe was incorporated as a non-profit organization and continues as the official sponsor.  The Washington Mardi Gras has grown to a three-day series of events that highlight the state’s food and culture, hosted by Louisiana’s members of Congress.  It features multiple parties, attendance of queens of Louisiana’s festivals, and the presentation of the king and queen and Mardi Gras princesses, most of whom are drawn from Louisiana families.  The ball is completely self-sustaining with costs covered by the sale of tickets, corporate donations and krewe memberships. Rex, 1875.	Krewe of Rex (Organization)	1875	Krewe of Rex (Organization); New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.	[14] p. : ill. ; 36 x 48 cm.	The Rex Organization was founded in 1872 in an effort to entertain Russia's Grand Duke Romanoff during his visit to the city, to attract visitors to New Orleans, and to provide a daytime parade as an alternative to the rowdy processions that had come to characterize Mardi Gras celebrations.  The following year, it began the tradition of holding a ball and selecting a Queen of Carnival.   Rex continues; its parade is held on the Mardi Gras day. Krewe of Babylon program, 1941.	Krewe of Babylon (Organization)	1941	Krewe of Babylon (Organization); Balls (Parties)--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.; New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.; New Orleans (La.)--Description and travel.; Tourism--Louisiana--New Orleans.	Program ; 22 cm.	The Jester’s Club, the sponsoring organization of the Knights of Babylon, was founded on June 24, 1939.  Babylon is a parading krewe and holds a ball with tableaux. Krewe of Rex admit card, 1920.	Krewe of Rex (Organization)	1920	Krewe of Rex (Organization); Carnival--Louisiana--New Orleans.; Balls (Parties)--Louisiana--New Orleans.; New Orleans (La.)--Social life and customs.	Invitation ; 15 cm.	The Rex Organization was founded in 1872 in an effort to entertain Russia's Grand Duke Romanoff during his visit to the city, to attract visitors to New Orleans, and to provide a daytime parade as an alternative to the rowdy processions that had come to characterize Mardi Gras celebrations.  The following year, it began the tradition of holding a ball and selecting a Queen of Carnival. Rex continues its parade is held on the Mardi Gras day.	Louisiana State University Libraries, Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	Finding aid: http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special/findaid/4785.pdf	32:134 Box 3	Charles L.
